## Communication

**How to write it:** Communication technology shapes the rhythm of relationships. When letters take weeks, show the ache of waiting — checking the post, rereading old letters until the paper wears thin, the agony of not knowing. When a message arrives, slow down: the recognition of handwriting, the decision whether to open it immediately or save it for privacy. Delayed communication creates dramatic irony (the reader knows what the character doesn't) and misunderstandings that have time to fester. Fast magical communication creates different tension: the pressure to respond immediately, the inability to hide behind distance, the intimacy of instant connection. Whatever your technology, show characters adapting their behavior around its constraints — the coded language because letters might be intercepted, the frustration when urgent news can't travel fast enough.

#### What communication methods exist over distance?

*Communication technology shapes the ache of separation. Can your characters reach each other across distance - and at what cost?*

| Method | Speed | Reliability | Privacy |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Courier/postal system | 3-7 days between major cities | Reasonably reliable; royal post is faster but expensive | Low — anyone can read it en route; use codes for secrets |
| Magical communication | Instant for bonded pairs | Perfect between bonded items; requires rare enchantment | High — only the bonded holder can activate it |
| Hand-delivered letters |  |  |  |
| Courier/postal system |  |  |  |
| Messenger birds |  |  |  |
| Signal systems (fire, flags) |  |  |  |
| Magical communication |  |  |  |
|  |  |  |  |
|  |  |  |  |
|  |  |  |  |

#### How long does it take to send a message between important locations?

*Delayed messages create dramatic irony and miscommunication. What might change before a letter arrives?*

| Route | Time |
| --- | --- |
| Between major cities |  |
| Between your characters when separated |  |

## Privacy & Surveillance

**How to write it:** Privacy scarcity makes intimacy precious. Show characters acutely aware of who might hear, see, or walk in. The constant listening for footsteps outside a door. The hushed voice that carries anyway. The relief of finally, finally being alone — and then not knowing what to do with the privacy they've craved. When characters lack privacy, show how they create it: the coded glance, the conversation held in plain sight that means something entirely different than the words suggest, the brief moment behind a pillar or in a crowd. When privacy is suddenly available, that shift should feel significant — the door that locks, the empty room, the space where they can speak freely for the first time. Privacy isn't just absence of watchers; it's the psychological shift when characters can stop performing.

#### How private are domestic spaces?

*Wall thickness, separate rooms, who shares space:*

[Your answer here]

#### Do locks exist? Who has them?

*The ability to lock a door is the ability to create private space. Who in your world has that power?*

[Your answer here]

#### Who has access to private spaces?

*Servants, family members, landlords, officials:*

[Your answer here]

#### What surveillance exists?

*Magical scrying? Spy networks? Informants? Nothing systematic?*

[Your answer here]

#### Where can people have truly private conversations?

*In a world where privacy is scarce, where do your characters go when they need to speak without being heard?*

[Your answer here]

#### What are the consequences of being overheard?

*The stakes of privacy shape how carefully characters speak. What would happen if the wrong person heard the wrong thing?*

## Lighting

**How to write it:** Lighting shapes the emotional tone of every scene. Candlelight is soft, flattering, creates shadows and intimacy — faces half-lit, features rendered gentle. Torchlight is harsher, flickering, creates drama and unease. Daylight reveals everything; characters can't hide in full sun. Use lighting to control what characters can and can't see: the moment of recognition when they step into light, the anonymity of darkness, the way firelight makes a familiar face look strange. Dim light forces proximity — leaning closer to see, speaking softer because darkness feels private. When characters are together in the dark, describe what other senses become heightened: sound, touch, the awareness of warmth from another body. The practical realities matter too: candles gutter and die, someone must tend the fire, darkness comes whether you're ready or not.

#### How do people light their spaces?

*Candles, oil lamps, torches, magical light, gas, electricity:*

[Your answer here]

#### How expensive is lighting?

*Can everyone afford to stay up after dark, or is darkness the norm for the poor?*

[Your answer here]

#### What does nighttime look like?

*Darkness creates different moods in different settings - danger in unlighted streets, intimacy in candlelit rooms, isolation in rural darkness.*

| Location | Lighting at Night |
| --- | --- |
| In cities |  |
| In homes |  |
| In the countryside |  |

#### What can and can't be done after dark?

*Darkness limits and enables. Some activities become impossible; others - secret meetings, escapes, confessions - become easier.*

[Your answer here]

| Element | Your World |
| --- | --- |

| Communication speed |  |

| Privacy level |  |
| Servant presence |  |
| Medical capabilities |  |
| Contraception availability |  |
| Documentation requirements |  |
| Technology gap between characters |  |

> ### Final Thought: Technology Defines What's Possible
>
> Your technology level determines what's easy and what's impossible. If instant communication exists, separation loses weight. If healing magic fixes anything, danger has no teeth. If documentation doesn't exist, identity can be fluid. If privacy is impossible, intimacy becomes a risk.
>
> Choose your technology level deliberately: Slow travel makes distance meaningful. Limited communication creates longing and uncertainty. Lack of privacy forces discretion. Limited medicine makes injuries matter. Absent documentation allows secrets.
>
> Technology isn't about gadgets — it's about what your world makes easy and what it makes hard. Build a technology level that creates the constraints your story needs, then let your characters navigate those constraints.

# Section 10

# Time, Seasons & Calendar

Time shapes everything — when people wake and sleep, when they celebrate, when crops are planted and harvested, when your characters can steal private moments. Understanding how your world measures time helps you create a sense of rhythm and place.

You don't need to invent an elaborate calendar system unless it matters to your story. What you do need is enough detail to make your world feel like it has history and seasons.

### In This Section

- [Measuring Time](#s10-time-measuring)
- [The Calendar](#s10-calendar)
- [Seasons & Weather](#s10-seasons)
- [Special Times & Significant Dates](#s10-special-times)

## Measuring Time

Different cultures measure time differently. Some count from a great event; others track the reign of monarchs. The way your world marks years says something about what it values.

#### How do people in your world measure time?

*Hours marked by bells? Sun position? Magical timekeepers? Water clocks? Does precision matter to ordinary people?*

[Your answer here]

#### How long is a day? Is it the same as Earth's 24 hours?

*Most fantasy uses Earth-standard time, but you can change this. Just be consistent.*

[Your answer here]

#### What do people call the parts of the day?

*Morning, noon, evening? Or something more evocative? "The golden hour," "the long watch," "shadowfall"?*

| Time Period | What It's Called |
| --- | --- |
| Dawn | "First light," "the waking hour" |
| Midday | "High sun," "the resting hour" |
| Dawn/Morning |  |
| Midday |  |
| Afternoon |  |
| Evening/Dusk |  |
| Night |  |
|  |  |
|  |  |
|  |  |

## The Calendar

Calendars organize the year. They tell people when to plant, when to celebrate, when to mourn. Your calendar doesn't need to be complex, but knowing the basics helps ground your story in a sense of passing time.

### Reference: Calendar Naming Ideas

*Use these patterns to create evocative month and day names for your world.*

| Naming Pattern | Examples |
| --- | --- |
| **Nature/Weather** | Frostmoon, Stormfall, Windsong, Firemist, Thaw, Harvest, Snowveil, Bloomtide |
| **Agricultural** | Sowing, Reaping, Planting Moon, Brewing Month, Shearing Time, Slaughter Moon |
| **Celestial** | Starmarch, Moondark, Sunpeak, Evenstar, Twilight Month, Shadow's Turn |
| **Religious/Mythic** | God's Rest, Prophet's Month, The Vigil, Saint's Tide, Blessing Moon, Atonement |
| **Historical Events** | Founding, Remembrance, Victory Month, The Mourning, Treaty's End, War's Wake |
| **Animals** | Wolf Moon, Stag Month, Raven's Turn, Bear Sleep, Eagle's Flight, Serpent's Rise |
| **Named for Rulers** | King's Month, Empress Tide, The Regent's Season, First Queen's Moon |
| **Ordinal/Numbered** | Firstmoon, Secondsun, Seventh Turn, Tenthwatch, The Long Month |

*Day names often follow similar patterns: Moonday, Starday, Fireday, Restday, Market Day, Temple Day.*

#### How many days are in a week? What are they called?

*Seven is common, but not required. Are days named for gods, elements, or something else?*

[Your answer here]

#### How many months are in a year? What are they called?

*You can use familiar names, invent new ones, or simply reference seasons. Pick what serves your story.*

| Month/Period | Season | Named For |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Frostmoon | Deep winter | The time of deepest cold when the moon seems frozen |
| Sowing | Early spring | When fields are planted |
|  |  |  |
|  |  |  |
|  |  |  |
|  |  |  |
|  |  |  |
|  |  |  |
|  |  |  |

#### How do people count years?

*From a founding event? A religious moment? The current ruler's reign? How old is your world by its own reckoning?*

[Your answer here]

#### What year does your story take place?

*By your world's calendar, when is this happening?*

[Your answer here]

## Seasons & Weather

Seasons affect everything from clothing to mood to travel. They determine when wars can be fought and when lovers might sneak away to gardens. Know your seasons.

#### How many seasons does your world have?

*The familiar four? Only wet and dry? Six distinct seasons? Something tied to magical cycles?*

[Your answer here]

#### What season does your story primarily take place in?

*Season affects mood, imagery, what characters wear, and what activities are possible.*

[Your answer here]

#### How does the season affect your characters' lives?

*Winter might trap them indoors together. Summer might mean war campaigns. Harvest might mean everyone's too busy for romance.*

[Your answer here]

Some moments in time carry weight. The anniversary of a battle, the day magic was born, the night when the veil between worlds thins. These can become important to your plot or your characters' personal histories.

# Section 10

# Building Your Magic System — The Foundation

Magic is often what makes a fantasy world feel like *fantasy*. But magic that can do anything is magic that means nothing. The most memorable magic systems have rules, costs, and limits—and those constraints are what make them interesting. When your character reaches for their power, we need to know what they're risking, what they're capable of, and what's completely beyond them.

This section builds your magic from the ground up: where it comes from, who can use it, how it works, and—most importantly—what it *can't* do. Get this foundation right, and your magic will feel real. Skip it, and you'll find yourself writing your way into corners or solving problems too easily.

One more thing before we dive in: magic in romantasy isn't just about battles and plot problems. It's also about *intimacy*—how your characters connect, what they hide from each other, what it means when they finally let someone see their power (or their vulnerability). As you build your system, keep one eye on how magic might bring your leads together or push them apart.

## In This Section

### Part One: The Foundation

- [Reference: Types of Magic Systems](#s10-types)
- [The Source](#s10-source)
- [Who Can Use Magic](#s10-who-can-use)
- [How Magic Works](#s10-how-works)
- [The Cost](#s10-cost)
- [The Limits](#s10-limits)
- [Scale and Power](#s10-scale-power)
- [Types and Specializations](#s10-specializations)
- [Hard Magic vs. Soft Magic](#s10-hard-soft)

### Part Two: Magic & Story

- [Magic in Your Story](#s10-story)
- [Consistency Check](#s10-consistency)

## Reference: Types of Magic Systems

Magic doesn't have to mean spellcasting. Here are different approaches to inspire you—mix and match, or invent your own.

| Type | How It Works | Example |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Elemental** | Control over natural forces (fire, water, earth, air) | Avatar, The Priory of the Orange Tree |
| **Spellcasting** | Words, gestures, or rituals produce specific effects | Harry Potter, The Name of the Wind |
| **Innate/Inborn** | Powers you're born with, often tied to bloodline | X-Men, Graceling, Ninth House |
| **Blood/Sacrifice** | Power drawn from blood, pain, or giving something up | Blood and Ash, Daughter of No Worlds |
| **Emotional/Will-Based** | Magic fueled by feelings, desire, or force of will | The Rage of Dragons |
| **Bond-Based** | Magic tied to a connection with another being | Fourth Wing, His Dark Materials |
| **Artifact-Based** | Power resides in objects, not people | Lord of the Rings |
| **Transformation** | Ability to change form | ACOTAR (shifting) |
| **Necromancy** | Power over death, spirits, or life's boundary | Gideon the Ninth, Sabriel |
| **Bargain/Contract** | Power gained through deals or binding agreements | ACOTAR (bargains) |

| Type | How It Works | Example |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Symbiotic/Parasitic** | Magic requires or is enhanced by another being | Venom, The Fifth Season |
| **Music/Art-Based** | Creation through song, art, or expression | Wintersong |
| **True Names** | Power from knowing the true nature of things | Earthsea, The Name of the Wind |
| **Psychic/Mental** | Mind-reading, telekinesis, mental influence | Shatter Me, Carrie |

#### Which type(s) best describe your magic system?

*You can combine multiple approaches.*

[Your answer here]

#### If your system doesn't fit these categories, describe what makes it different:

*Unique magic systems are memorable. What makes yours distinctive from what readers have seen before?*

[Your answer here]

## The Source

Every magic system has an origin—where the power actually comes from. This shapes everything: who has access, how it's viewed by society, and what it costs to use.

#### Where does magic come from in your world?

*Options: the gods or divine forces, the natural world (ley lines, elemental forces), an internal source (bloodlines, souls, emotions), external objects, knowledge and study, a bargain or bond, something unknown or mysterious.*

[Your answer here]

#### Is there a single source of magic, or multiple types with different origins?

*If multiple, how do they interact—or conflict?*

[Your answer here]

#### Can the source be depleted, corrupted, or cut off? What happens if it is?

*Vulnerable magic sources create stakes. What would your protagonist do if their power began to fail?*

[Your answer here]

#### How do people in your world explain where magic comes from?

*Is the truth different from what most believe?*

[Your answer here]

> *#### Romantasy Check: Could the source of magic connect your leads—or divide them?
>
> Sometimes magic creates multiple layers of division. In *ACOTAR*: Feyre is human; Tamlin is High Fae. That's the obvious gap—she's mortal and powerless in his world. But there's also something he's not telling her. The reader experiences the divide as a mystery: *why won't he tell me the truth?*
>
> Or the division might be more straightforward: Magic runs through noble bloodlines, and she's aristocracy while he's common-born—except he's developing abilities that shouldn't exist in someone like him.*

#### How might the source of magic affect your leads' relationship?

*Magic's origin can unite or divide. Do your characters share the same source, or does their magic come from opposing places?*

[Your answer here]

## Who Can Use Magic

Not everyone has to be magical—and who *can* wield magic shapes everything from social structure to your protagonist's place in the world.

#### How common is magic in your world?

*Can nearly everyone use some form? Limited to certain bloodlines, species, or chosen ones? Can anyone learn it with training? Vanishingly rare?*

[Your answer here]

#### What determines whether someone can use magic?

*Birth (bloodlines, species, being "chosen"), training and study, a triggering event (trauma, ritual), possession of an object or bond, random chance, a sacrifice or bargain.*

[Your answer here]

#### Can magical ability be gained if you weren't born with it? Can it be lost or taken away?

*The permanence of magical ability affects what characters fear and hope for. Could your protagonist gain power - or lose everything?*

[Your answer here]

#### If magic is inherited, how does that affect families, dynasties, and marriages?

*If it's learned, who controls access to that knowledge—and who's excluded?*

[Your answer here]

> *#### Romantasy Check: How does who can use magic affect the dynamic between your leads?
>
> In *Serpent & Dove*: Lou is a witch hiding her magic; Reid is a witch hunter sworn to kill her kind. It's not just that one has magic and one doesn't—it's that his entire identity is built on destroying what she is. The question isn't just "who has power"—it's "what happens when he finds out?"*

#### How does magical access (or lack of it) shape the dynamic between your leads?

*Power imbalances create tension. How do your characters navigate differences in magical ability?*

| Aspect | Details |
| --- | --- |
| Protagonist's magical status | Latent power, newly awakened; untrained but potentially immense; she's only beginning to understand what she can do |
| Love Interest's magical status | Fully trained, centuries of control; he's considered one of the most powerful mages alive but hides the true extent |
| What this means for their dynamic | He could easily overpower her — so he holds back; she resents being protected but also fears hurting him if she loses control |
| Protagonist's magical status |  |
| Love Interest's magical status |  |
| What this means for their dynamic |  |
|  |  |
|  |  |
|  |  |

## How Magic Works

This is the mechanical heart of your system—the "physics" of magic. You don't need to explain everything to readers, but *you* should understand how it operates so your story stays consistent.

#### How does someone actually do magic? What does the process look like?

*Spoken words, physical gestures, intense concentration, drawing symbols, channeling through objects, emotional states, rituals, physical contact, visualization, music or art.*

[Your answer here]

#### What does magic look like when it happens?

*What do bystanders see, hear, or feel?*

[Your answer here]

#### How long does it take to use magic?

*Can it be done instantly, or does it require preparation?*

[Your answer here]

#### Can magic be interrupted? What happens if it's disrupted mid-use?

*Interruptible magic creates vulnerability during casting - a moment when the powerful become defenseless.*

[Your answer here]

#### Is magic precise or unpredictable?

*Does the same action always produce the same result, or is there variation based on skill, emotion, or circumstance?*

[Your answer here]

> *#### Romantasy Check: Is there anything about how magic is performed that creates vulnerability or intimacy?
>
> In *Fourth Wing*: Dragon riders share a mental bond with their dragons—and sometimes with each other. Violet and Xaden can speak mind-to-mind, which sounds romantic until you realize it means he knows when she's scared, when she's lying, when she's thinking about him. There's nowhere to hide. The bond doesn't just connect them; it strips away the walls they've both built.*

#### How might the process of using magic create vulnerable or intimate moments between your leads?

*The physical or emotional demands of casting can strip away defenses. What might your characters reveal when magic leaves them exposed?*

[Your answer here]

## The Cost

This is where your magic system gets genuinely interesting. Unlimited power is boring; power with a price creates drama. What does magic take from the user—and is it worth paying?

#### What does using magic cost?

*Physical energy/exhaustion, pain/damage, shortened lifespan, emotional toll, rare materials, time, moral cost (corruption, debt), something from the world around them.*

[Your answer here]

#### Does the cost scale with the power used?

*Is a small spell a small price, while world-shaking magic demands everything?*

[Your answer here]

#### What happens when someone overextends—uses more magic than they can safely handle?

*Overextension consequences create tension in high-stakes moments. What would your protagonist risk by pushing too far?*

[Your answer here]

#### Is the cost immediate, or does it accumulate over time?

*Can someone use magic freely for years and then pay all at once?*

[Your answer here]

#### Are there situational or plot-driven costs—times when magic can't be used safely?

*In *ACOTAR*: Rhysand limits his magic use because the enemy can track it. Think about: Can magic be traced? Would using it alert enemies or violate a treaty? Does magic leave evidence?*

[Your answer here]

#### Does your protagonist know the full cost of their power, or will they find out the hard way?

*Hidden costs create devastating revelations. What might your protagonist discover about the price they've been paying - or will pay?*

[Your answer here]

> *#### Romantasy Check: How might the cost of magic create romantic tension or sacrifice?
>
> In *From Blood and Ash*: Poppy's gift lets her sense others' emotions and take away their pain—but it means absorbing that pain into herself. Every time she helps someone, she suffers for it. When she uses her power on Hawke, she's not just healing him; she's choosing to hurt for him.
>
> Or: His power is fueled by strong emotion, which means falling in love makes him more powerful but also more dangerous. Or: Magic costs memories, and she's starting to forget why she's fighting—including starting to forget him.*

#### How might the cost of magic create stakes in the relationship?

*When magic demands sacrifice, what would one character pay to protect the other - and what would the other feel about that price?*

[Your answer here]

## The Limits

What magic *cannot* do is more important than what it can. Limits create stakes, force creativity, and prevent your characters from solving every problem with a wave of their hand.

#### What is absolutely impossible with magic in your world? Name at least three things.

*Firm limitations prevent magic from solving every problem. What must your characters face without magical shortcuts?*

[Your answer here]

### Reference: Types of Magic Limitations

| Limitation Type | Examples | Story Function |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Impossible Acts** | Can't raise the dead, can't create love, can't time travel | Some problems must be solved without magic |
| **Material Weaknesses** | Iron disrupts fae, silver harms werewolves, salt breaks enchantments | Gives non-magical characters a chance |
| **Environmental** | Fails in certain locations/times | Creates dangerous/safe spaces |
| **Physical State** | Can't use when exhausted, injured, or emotional | Physical danger matters to mages |
| **Knowledge/Skill** | Must learn abilities, years of training required | Creates expertise hierarchies |
| **Resource Depletion** | Energy runs out, components consumed, limited uses | Creates tactical decisions |

| Limitation Type | Examples | Story Function |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Backlash** | Overuse causes damage, failed magic backfires, corruption | Makes magical choices risky |
| **Range/Scale** | Only affects what you see/touch, power diminishes with distance | Keeps magic personal |
| **Countermeasures** | Others can block/dispel, wards exist, immunities | Creates strategic depth |
| **Social/Legal** | Magic is illegal, regulated, taboo | External conflict beyond magic |
| **Specificity** | Fire mages can't do ice, each person has one gift | Requires teamwork |
| **Consent/Will** | Can't affect someone who truly resists | Protects character agency |

#### Which limitation types exist in your system?

*Every limitation creates story opportunities. Which constraints will force your characters to be creative, vulnerable, or dependent on others?*

[Your answer here]

#### Are there things magic can technically do, but no one attempts because the cost or risk is too high?

*Forbidden-but-possible magic creates temptation. What might your protagonist be desperate enough to try?*

[Your answer here]

#### Can magic be resisted or defended against?

*How do non-magical people protect themselves?*

[Your answer here]

> *#### Romantasy Check: Do any of your limitations create romantic complications?
>
> In *The Cruel Prince*: The Fae cannot lie. Every cruel thing Cardan says, Jude knows he means. And every rare moment of honesty hits harder because she knows it's true; he literally cannot say "I love you" unless he does. The limitation forces them to become masters of misdirection and half-truths.*

#### How might your magic's limitations affect the relationship?

*Limitations can protect or obstruct love. Can magic reveal truth, or does it force lies? Does it prevent harm, or make protection impossible?*

[Your answer here]

## Scale and Power

Not all magic users are created equal. Understanding the range of power helps you place your characters and set stakes appropriately.

#### What's the range of magical power in your world?

*Understanding power's spectrum helps you position your characters - and creates context for whether their abilities are remarkable or ordinary.*

| Level | Description |
| --- | --- |
| Weakest magic user |  |
| Strongest magic user |  |

#### Where do your protagonist and love interest fall on this scale?

*Their relative power positions create dynamics. Is one vastly stronger? Are they evenly matched? Does it even out in unexpected ways?*

| Character | Power Level |
| --- | --- |
| Protagonist |  |
| Love Interest |  |

#### Is raw power the only measure of magical strength?

*Or can skill, creativity, knowledge, or cleverness make a "weaker" user formidable?*

[Your answer here]

#### What's the most impressive feat of magic in your world's history?

*Could anyone alive today replicate it?*

[Your answer here]

#### Is magical power fixed, or can it grow?

*How does someone become more powerful—and what do they risk in pursuing that growth?*

[Your answer here]

> *#### Romantasy Check: If there's a power gap between your leads, how do you balance the relationship?
>
> In later *ACOTAR* books: Rhysand is the most powerful High Lord in history. But the story doesn't let that gap make Feyre irrelevant—she has things he needs that have nothing to do with magic: she sees through his masks, she challenges his decisions. Power isn't just magic—it's also who's willing to call you on your bullshit.*

#### If there's a power gap, what does the less powerful person bring that the powerful one needs?

*Balanced relationships require more than magical equality. What does each character offer that the other cannot provide for themselves?*

[Your answer here]

## Types and Specializations

Some worlds have one kind of magic; others have many flavors. Understanding whether your magic is unified or diverse affects how characters relate to their powers—and to each other.

#### Is magic in your world one unified force, or are there distinct types, schools, or disciplines?

*Different magical traditions can create cultural divides or opportunities for complementary partnership. If there are distinct types, list them.*

[Your answer here]

#### Do magic users specialize, or can someone master multiple types?

*What determines their specialty—birth, choice, training, or something else?*

[Your answer here]

#### Are some types of magic considered more valuable, dangerous, or taboo than others?

*Stigmatized magic creates secrets to hide or discover. Does either character possess abilities they must conceal?*

[Your answer here]

#### Do different types of magic interact?

*Can they combine for greater effect, cancel each other out, or create unexpected reactions?*

[Your answer here]

> *#### Romantasy Check: How do your leads' magic types interact?
>
> In *Gideon the Ninth*: Harrow is a necromancer—she works with bones and death. Gideon is her cavalier, a swordswoman with no magic. The magic demands partnership; their history demands distance. The tension is about two people who are magically designed to be partners but emotionally unable to trust each other.*

#### How might your leads' types of magic interact—for good or ill?

*Complementary magic can create partnership; conflicting magic can create danger or forbidden attraction.*

| Aspect | Details |
| --- | --- |
| Protagonist's magic |  |
| Love Interest's magic |  |
| How they might clash |  |
| How they might complement |  |

## Hard Magic vs. Soft Magic: Where Does Your System Land?

**Hard Magic** has clearly defined rules, costs, and limitations. Readers understand what magic can and can't do, so magical solutions feel earned.

**Soft Magic** is mysterious and not fully explained. It creates wonder and danger. The risk: solving major problems with undefined magic can feel like cheating.

**Most romantasy falls somewhere in between**—defined enough for stakes, mysterious enough for wonder.

**How to write it:** For hard magic, show the rules through consequence. Don't explain that healing magic requires equivalent pain — show the healer gritting their teeth, show the price paid. For soft magic, maintain consistency in mood and limitation: if magic feels dangerous and unpredictable, keep that feeling; don't let it become convenient when needed. In both cases, write magic through the body: the physical sensation of drawing power, the exhaustion after use, the way it feels to be on the receiving end. When your character tests their limits, show the attempt, the strain, and the moment they hit the boundary — whether that's a rule they can't break or a cost they can't pay. Magic becomes real when readers feel its weight.

#### Where does your magic fall on the spectrum?

*HARD (Clear rules) ←――――――――――→ SOFT (Mysterious, wondrous)*

[Your answer here]

#### If your magic is on the harder side: Have you established the rules clearly enough that readers will accept magical solutions?

*Hard magic requires setup. The abilities your protagonist uses to solve problems must be demonstrated beforehand.*

[Your answer here]

#### If your magic is on the softer side: Are you avoiding using vague magic to solve major plot problems?

*Soft magic works better for creating problems than solving them. Deus ex magica feels like cheating.*

[Your answer here]

#### If you're in the middle: Which elements are rule-bound and which are mysterious?

*Be consistent about what the reader understands vs. what remains wondrous. Clarity about your character's abilities; mystery about the larger world.*

[Your answer here]

## Magic in Your Story

You've built the system. Now let's make sure it actually *works* for the story you're telling—both the plot and the romance.

### Magic and Plot

#### How does magic create or complicate your central conflict?

*Not just "there's a magical villain"—how do the *rules* of your magic shape what's possible?*

[Your answer here]

#### What can your antagonist do with magic that makes them a genuine threat?

*What limits prevent them from simply winning immediately?*

[Your answer here]

### Act 1: Setup — The Inciting Incident

In *ACOTAR*: Feyre kills a faerie—a magical creature—in the woods. The inciting incident isn't just "something happens"; it's "something magical happens that she can't undo."

#### What magical event, ability, or consequence pulls your protagonist out of their ordinary world?

*The inciting incident often involves magic working in ways the protagonist didn't expect or couldn't control.*

[Your answer here]

#### How does this same magical event connect them to the love interest?

*In romantasy, the fantasy inciting incident and the meet-cute should be linked.*

[Your answer here]

### Act 2: Rising Action — Building Tension

In *ACOTAR*: As Feyre spends time in the Spring Court, she's surrounded by magic she doesn't understand. The curse is ticking down, adding urgency Tamlin can't explain. Magic isn't just backdrop; it's pressure.

#### What magical obstacles, revelations, or complications arise as your leads grow closer?

*Magic should complicate the romance as much as it complicates the plot - secrets about power, dangerous abilities, conflicting duties.*

[Your answer here]

#### Does magic create intimacy or distance as they grow closer?

*Shared power, training together, magical bonds forming? Or secrets, power imbalances, dangerous abilities?*

[Your answer here]

### Act 3: Crisis — Everything Falls Apart

In *ACOTAR*: Feyre is powerless among the most powerful beings in the world, Tamlin is bound and can't help her. The very magic that drew them together now seems to make saving each other impossible.

#### What magical crisis makes everything seem hopeless?

*How does magic trap, separate, or endanger your leads at their lowest point?*

[Your answer here]

### Act 4: Resolution — The Climax

In *ACOTAR*: Feyre solves Amarantha's riddle, and the answer is "love." Her willingness to die for Tamlin breaks the curse. The romantic sacrifice triggers the magical solution. The romantic climax IS the magical climax.

#### How does your protagonist's romantic choice enable the magical resolution?

*In the best romantasy, love is not separate from magic - the emotional climax and the magical climax should intertwine.*

[Your answer here]

#### What is your protagonist's magical state at the end versus the beginning?

*Gained power, lost it, transformed, or learned to use it differently?*

[Your answer here]

### Magic and Your World

#### How has magic shaped the power structures in your world?

*Who's on top because of magic—and who's at the bottom?*

[Your answer here]

#### What do non-magical people think of magic users?

*Fear? Reverence? Resentment? Envy? Exploitation?*

[Your answer here]

### Magic and Romance

#### Does your magic system include any bonds, bargains, or connections between people?

*Soul bonds, mating marks, magical contracts, shared power?*

[Your answer here]

#### If you have magical bonds: Are they chosen or fated?

*Can they be broken? What does your story say about destiny vs. choice?*

[Your answer here]

#### How might magic create obstacles between your leads?

*Forbidden types of magic, power imbalances, magic that makes trust difficult, duties that pull them apart, being on opposite sides.*

[Your answer here]

#### How might magic create connection between your leads?

*Shared abilities or training, one can help/heal/protect the other, magical communication, complementary powers, using magic together creates intimacy.*

[Your answer here]

#### What would it mean for your protagonist to use their magic for their love interest in a personal, private way?

*Protective, generous, or revealing something they usually hide:*

[Your answer here]

#### What would it mean for your protagonist to use their magic in front of their love interest in a way they don't show others?

*Revealing their full power, their vulnerability, or a secret aspect of their abilities:*

[Your answer here]

## Consistency Check

Before you move on, let's make sure your magic system holds together.

#### Write out your magic system in two or three sentences:

*This summary should capture the essence of your magic: source, who can use it, how it works, main cost, and biggest limit. If you can't summarize it clearly, the system may need simplification.*

[Your answer here]

#### Does your magic system contradict itself anywhere?

*For example: "Magic is extremely rare" but also "Every noble family has a court mage."*

[Your answer here]

#### Think of the biggest problem your protagonist faces.

*If a skeptical reader asked "Why didn't they just use magic to fix that?" - what's your answer? Good limitations create good answers.*

[Your answer here]

#### What's one thing you're still unsure about in your magic system?

*Write it down—you may figure it out as you draft, or in later sections.*

[Your answer here]

> ### Final Thought: Magic Is About Choices
>
> The best magic systems aren't about power—they're about cost, consequence, and choice. Every time your character reaches for their magic, they should be weighing what they gain against what they risk.
>
> Magic in romantasy should create both obstacles and opportunities for connection. It can divide your leads (forbidden powers, opposite sides, dangerous secrets) or unite them (shared abilities, complementary gifts, the vulnerability of showing someone your true power).
>
> Build magic that forces your characters to make hard choices—and makes readers feel the weight of those choices.

# Section 11

# Magic & Intimacy

Here's a trap many romantasy writers fall into: they design a magic system, then bolt on something "intimate" — a telepathic bond, a touch-based power transfer, a soul link that lets characters feel each other's emotions. These mechanics aren't inherently bad, but they're heavy-handed. They make the magic do the romantic work instead of the characters.

The truth is, *any* magic system can create intimacy. It's not about what the magic *is* — it's about how your characters *choose to use it.*

Think about Rhysand in ACOTAR. His winnowing ability is transportation and summoning magic — nothing inherently romantic about it. But he uses it to send Feyre notes, appearing and disappearing paper and pen so they can have a private conversation across distance. The intimacy isn't built into the magic. It comes from the choice to use his power *that way*, to create something private that belongs only to them.

> *#### This is the real question:
>
> **Given the magic your characters already have, how might they use it to reach each other?***

## In This Section

### Part One: Magic as Intimate Language

- [The Intimate Application](#s11-intimate-application)
- [Small Uses, Big Meaning](#s11-small-uses)
- [Private Channels](#s11-private-channels)
- [How Magic Reveals Character](#s11-reveals-character)
- [Vulnerability Through Magic](#s11-vulnerability)

### Part Two: Bonds & Fated Connection

- [Direct Intimate Magic: Bonds, Marks & Fated Connection](#s11-direct-intimate)
- [Magical vs. Emotional Intimacy](#s11-magical-emotional)
- [The Agency Check](#s11-agency-check)

## The Intimate Application

Look at the magic system you've already built. Don't add new "romantic" mechanics — instead, find the intimate potential in what exists.

#### What magic does your protagonist have?

*List their abilities without thinking about romance yet.*

[Your answer here]

#### Now: how could this magic be used to create a private moment?

*A secret gesture? A communication no one else would notice or understand?*

[Your answer here]

#### What about your love interest's magic?

*What could they do with their abilities that would feel personal, specific, meant only for your protagonist?*

[Your answer here]

#### Is there something one character's magic could do for the other that would be difficult, costly, or unusual for them?

*Making the gesture more meaningful:*

[Your answer here]

## Small Uses, Big Meaning

Grand magical gestures are easy to spot. The interesting stuff is smaller — the ways magic becomes part of a private language between two people.

#### What repeated small gesture might develop between your characters using their magic?

*Think about: a fire mage who always keeps a candle lit in someone's window; an illusionist who makes small images appear to make the other laugh; a weather worker who clears the rain from just the space where someone's standing; a telekinetic who adjusts someone's collar without touching them.*

[Your answer here]

#### What magical gesture would your characters recognize as meaningful that others would overlook or misunderstand?

*Private meaning transforms ordinary magic into intimate language. What small act holds significance only for them?*

[Your answer here]

#### How might your character's magic show care in a way that words wouldn't?

*Especially if they're someone who struggles to express feelings directly:*

[Your answer here]

## Private Channels

One thing magic can do is create space for communication that exists outside normal channels — not because the magic is telepathic, but because your characters find ways to use it that way.

#### Do your characters have any way of communicating that others can't easily intercept?

*This doesn't have to be mind-reading. It could be: enchanted objects passed back and forth, messages hidden in magical constructs, illusions only one person can see, a shared spell that signals without words.*

[Your answer here]

#### What can they say through this channel that they couldn't say aloud or in public?

*What makes this form of communication feel safer?*

[Your answer here]

#### Did they create this private channel intentionally, or did it develop accidentally?

*What does its origin say about their relationship?*

[Your answer here]

## How Magic Reveals Character

The way someone uses magic shows who they are. In romance, this becomes a way for characters to *see* each other — to notice things about how the other person wields power that others miss.

#### What does the way your protagonist uses magic reveal about them that most people don't notice?

*Are they more gentle than they appear? More precise? More reckless? More afraid?*

[Your answer here]

#### What does the love interest notice about the protagonist's magic that others overlook?

*Seeing what others miss is a form of intimacy. What do they perceive that reveals how closely they watch?*

[Your answer here]

#### What do they see in each other's magic that makes them understand each other differently?

*Witnessing someone's magic can reveal who they truly are - their restraint, their passion, their fear, their care.*

[Your answer here]

#### Is there a moment where one character sees the other use magic and realizes something important?

*About their power, their control, their fear, their care:*

[Your answer here]

## Vulnerability Through Magic

Magic can strip away defenses — not because it's designed to, but because using it requires something from the person wielding it.

#### When is your character most vulnerable while using magic?

*During casting, after exhaustion, when emotions run high, when they're at their limits?*

[Your answer here]

#### What would it mean for the love interest to see them in that state?

*Is this something they'd normally hide?*

[Your answer here]

#### Has your character ever had to use magic in front of the love interest when they would have preferred to hide?

*What happened?*

[Your answer here]

#### Flip it: has your character ever seen the love interest vulnerable through magic?

*What did they learn?*

[Your answer here]

## Direct Intimate Magic: Bonds, Marks & Fated Connection

Some magic systems *do* include mechanics that directly link characters — mating bonds, soul marks, fated recognition, shared senses, dream connections. These tropes are popular for good reason: they offer certainty in a genre built on the question of "will they?" They promise that yes, these two belong together. The universe itself says so.

But that certainty is also the danger. When the magic declares two people are destined for each other before the characters (or readers) have any reason to believe it, the bond can feel like a shortcut — replacing the work of falling in love with a magical fait accompli.

> #### The Best Versions of Direct Intimate Magic
>
> The best versions treat the bond as a **complication**, not a conclusion. The magic might say they're matched, but it doesn't make them compatible. It doesn't resolve their conflicts, heal their wounds, or build trust. It just makes walking away harder.

### The Mechanics First

Before you think about what the bond means for your romance, you need to understand what it actually *is* in your world. A bond that's biological works differently than one that's divine. Get the mechanics clear first — the romantic implications will follow.

#### What is the bond, fundamentally? What kind of phenomenon is it?

*Is it biological (pheromones, genetic compatibility)? Magical (a spell, curse, enchantment)? Divine (granted by gods, written in fate)? Spiritual (souls recognizing each other)? Something your world doesn't fully understand?*

[Your answer here]

#### How does a bond form? What triggers it?

*Exists from birth? Snaps at first meeting/touch? Requires ritual or vow? Builds gradually? Can be created deliberately or only happens spontaneously?*

[Your answer here]

#### Is the bond universal in your world, or rare?

*Does everyone have a fated mate? Only certain bloodlines or species? Common enough for social customs, or rare enough they don't believe it at first?*

[Your answer here]

#### What is the bond's relationship to your broader magic system?

*Same rules, costs, limitations? Or operates outside normal magical laws?*

[Your answer here]

#### How much does your world understand about how bonds work?

*Well-studied? Shrouded in mystery? Actively suppressed? Will characters discover what they believed is wrong?*

[Your answer here]

### Types of Direct Connection

Different mechanics create different dynamics. Understanding what yours actually does helps you use it well.

#### What form does direct intimate magic take in your world?

*Mating bonds, soul marks, fated mate recognition through scent/sight/sensation, telepathic links, shared sensory experiences, dream-walking, magical contracts:*

[Your answer here]

#### What does the bond actually do? Be specific about the mechanics.

*Physical pull? Emotional awareness? Telepathy? Pain when separated? Recognition? Sexual compatibility?*

[Your answer here]

#### What doesn't the bond do? What's still missing even with this connection?

*The bond might create attraction but not trust. Recognition but not compatibility. Awareness but not understanding. What gaps remain?*

[Your answer here]

### Destiny vs. Choice

This is the core tension in any fated-connection story. Readers want to believe the couple belongs together, but they also want to believe the characters *chose* each other. Pure destiny can feel like a cage. Pure choice in a fated-bond world can feel like the magic doesn't matter.

> The sweet spot is usually: **the bond creates the opportunity or the pull, but the relationship requires choice.**

#### In your world, is the bond a compulsion, an invitation, or something in between?

*A compulsion leaves no room for choice. An invitation can be refused. Most interesting bonds live somewhere in the middle.*

[Your answer here]

#### Can the bond be rejected, resisted, or refused? What does that cost?

*Physical pain? Shortened lifespan? Loss of power? Endless longing? Social consequences? Nothing at all?*

[Your answer here]

#### Has anyone in your world rejected a bond? What happened to them?

*Stories of rejection establish stakes. Do cautionary tales make your characters more afraid - or more determined to resist?*

[Your answer here]

#### If your characters could walk away from the bond without consequence, would they still choose each other?

*At what point in the story does this become true?*

[Your answer here]

### When the Bond Reveals Itself

Timing changes everything. A bond recognized at first meeting creates different tension than one that emerges after feelings already exist.

#### When do your characters become aware of the bond?

*Before they have feelings for each other, or after?*

[Your answer here]

#### If the bond comes first: How do your characters interpret their growing feelings?

*Do they trust what they feel, or wonder if it's just the magic? How does this doubt create conflict?*

[Your answer here]

#### If feelings come first: How does discovering the bond change things?

*Confirmation or stolen choice? One validated while the other feels trapped?*

[Your answer here]

#### Do both characters discover the bond at the same time?

*Or does one know before the other? What does this asymmetry create?*

[Your answer here]

### The Inconvenient Bond

The most compelling fated-connection stories put the bond in direct conflict with everything else in the characters' lives. The magic pulls them together while circumstances, history, politics, or personality push them apart.

#### What makes this bond inconvenient, unwanted, or complicated for your protagonist?

*The love interest is an enemy, rival, captor, wrong species, wrong class, already committed, politically dangerous, personally infuriating, someone who hurt them or their people.*

[Your answer here]

#### What makes it inconvenient for your love interest?

*Both characters should have reasons to resist. What does the love interest stand to lose by accepting this connection?*

[Your answer here]

#### What would your characters lose by accepting the bond?

*Position, freedom, other relationships, sense of self, life goals?*

[Your answer here]

#### What are they fighting against when they resist?

*The bond itself, or what accepting it would mean for their lives?*

[Your answer here]

### The Work the Bond Doesn't Do

A bond might guarantee compatibility on some level, but it doesn't build a relationship. These questions help you identify what your characters still have to earn.

#### The bond might create attraction — but what about trust?

*What does each character have to do to earn the other's trust despite the bond?*

[Your answer here]

#### The bond might create recognition — but what about understanding?

*What do they still not know about each other that matters?*

[Your answer here]

#### The bond might say they're matched — but what about actual compatibility?

*Where do they clash, disagree, or drive each other crazy?*

[Your answer here]

#### What conflict exists between them that the bond cannot resolve?

*What would they be fighting about even without the magical connection?*

[Your answer here]

#### What wound does each character carry that the bond doesn't heal?

*How might the bond even make that wound more painful?*

[Your answer here]

### Visibility and Social Reality

Bonds exist in a social context. How others perceive and respond to the bond shapes what it means for your characters.

#### Is the bond visible to others?

*Can people see the mark, sense the connection, or recognize bonded pairs?*

[Your answer here]

#### How does your society view bonded pairs?

*Reverence, envy, suspicion, obligation, legal recognition, political value?*

[Your answer here]

#### Is their specific bond acceptable, or does who they're bonded to create scandal?

*Danger or political crisis?*

[Your answer here]

#### Can a bond be hidden?

*What would they have to do to conceal it, and what happens if they're discovered?*

[Your answer here]

### Bonds and Power

Intimate magic often creates power dynamics — who has more information, more control, more ability to affect the other.

#### Does the bond give one character more access or information than the other?

*One feels the other's emotions but not vice versa; one can find the other but not be found; one initiated the bond without consent.*

[Your answer here]

#### If the bond is asymmetrical, how does this create tension?

*How does the character with less power assert agency?*

[Your answer here]

#### Can the bond be used against one of the characters?

*Could an enemy exploit the connection?*

[Your answer here]

#### What would it mean for one character to "close off" or "shut down" their end of the bond?

*Is this possible? What would it feel like to the other?*

[Your answer here]

### The Choice Moment

Regardless of how fated the bond is, the most satisfying romantic payoff comes when characters *choose* each other — not because the magic compels them, but because they want this, consequences and all.

#### At what point do your characters stop fighting the bond and start choosing each other?

*What changes?*

[Your answer here]

#### What does choosing look like?

*Is there a moment, a declaration, an action that marks the shift from "stuck with this" to "I want this"?*

[Your answer here]

#### If the bond disappeared tomorrow, would they stay?

*At what point in your story does this become true?*

[Your answer here]

## Magical vs. Emotional Intimacy

This distinction matters whether your magic creates direct connection or not. Magic can create *access* without creating *trust*. It can create *exposure* without creating *understanding*.

#### What does magic give your characters access to in each other?

*What do they still have to earn the hard way through time, honesty, and choice?*

[Your answer here]

#### Can two people in your world be emotionally intimate without any magical component?

*What does purely human closeness look like against the backdrop of your magical world?*

[Your answer here]

#### What would your characters have if you stripped away all magical connection?

*Would there still be something between them?*

[Your answer here]

## The Agency Check

Magic should enhance your romance, not do the work for it. These questions help you make sure the characters are driving the connection.

#### If you removed every magical link between your characters, would they still have reasons to be drawn to each other?

*What are those reasons?*

[Your answer here]

#### When your characters connect through magic, is it because the magic compels it — or because they're choosing to use their magic to reach each other?

*The distinction matters. Compelled connection may feel intense, but chosen connection reveals character.*

[Your answer here]

#### At what point in your story do your characters choose each other as people?

*Not because of magical mechanics but despite the complications magic creates:*

[Your answer here]

> ### Final Thought: Magic Enhances, It Doesn't Replace
>
> The most romantic uses of magic aren't the ones built into the system — they're the ones your characters invent. Private gestures, secret communications, the choice to use power gently when gentleness isn't required.
>
> Whether your magic includes fated bonds or not, the real intimacy comes from characters choosing each other. The bond can say they're matched; only the characters can prove it true.

## Basic Words Template

You don't need to build a complete language. A handful of key words and phrases can add real flavor to your world.

These are the terms that come up most often in stories. Pick the ones that matter for your plot and characters, and don't worry about filling every row.

# Section 12

# Magic as Conflict Generator

Magic isn't just a tool for solving problems — it's one of the best sources of problems. The limits, dangers, and social consequences of magic can create exactly the kind of pressure that romance needs: secrets that must be kept, distances that must be maintained, power dynamics that must be negotiated.

This section is about how your magic system creates *obstacles* between your characters.

## In This Section

### Personal Magic Conflicts

- [Dangerous Power](#s12-dangerous-power)
- [Forbidden or Hunted Magic](#s12-forbidden)
- [Secrets & Hidden Costs](#s12-secrets)
- [Oaths, Debts & Binding Agreements](#s12-oaths)

### Relational Magic Conflicts

- [Opposition & Incompatibility](#s12-opposition)
- [Power Imbalance](#s12-power-imbalance)
- [Magic Used Against Will](#s12-against-will)

### Structural Magic Conflicts

- [The World at War: Magic as Structural Pressure](#s12-world-at-war)

## Dangerous Power

Magic that's difficult to control creates built-in tension: the fear of hurting someone you care about.

**How to write it:** Show danger through the character's constant physical awareness of their power — the way they hold themselves still, the reflexive clenching when emotions spike, the careful distance they maintain. Let readers see near-misses: the glass that cracks, the temperature drop, the flicker of something wrong that the character quickly suppresses. When they do lose control, even briefly, make the aftermath as important as the moment itself — the horror, the withdrawal, the way they won't look at the person they almost hurt. The romance tension comes from the partner moving closer while the dangerous one backs away, from learning to trust someone with proximity despite the risk. The first time the dangerous character lets the other person touch them during a moment of high emotion is a turning point — they're choosing trust over safety.

#### Is your character's magic dangerous to others? To themselves? To both?

*Consider how the specific nature of the danger shapes their daily life and relationships.*

[Your answer here]

#### Can this danger be managed with training, or is it inherent to the magic itself?

*What does "control" look like — and what does losing control look like?*

[Your answer here]

#### Has your character ever hurt someone with their magic?

*What happened, and how did it shape their relationship to their power?*

[Your answer here]

#### How does the fear of causing harm affect how your character lets people close?

*What protective distance do they maintain — and what would make them risk closing it?*

[Your answer here]

#### What would the love interest have to do or say to convince your character that the risk is worth taking?

*What proof would they need?*

[Your answer here]

## Forbidden or Hunted Magic

Some magic is outlawed, feared, or misunderstood. Characters who wield it carry a secret that can destroy them if revealed.

#### Is your character's magic forbidden, illegal, or socially condemned?

*What are the consequences of being discovered — execution, imprisonment, exile, experimentation?*

[Your answer here]

#### Who knows about their abilities? Who absolutely cannot find out?

*Think about the layers of secrecy and who your protagonist trusts with pieces of the truth.*

[Your answer here]

#### What does your character have to do to hide their magic?

*What daily deceptions, limitations, or sacrifices does concealment require?*

[Your answer here]

#### What would it mean to reveal their magic to the love interest?

*What's the worst-case outcome they fear? What's the hope they might not admit to?*

[Your answer here]

#### If the love interest discovered the truth by accident rather than being told, how would that affect trust?

*The difference between confession and discovery can define whether secrets become intimacy or betrayal.*

[Your answer here]

## Secrets & Hidden Costs

Beyond forbidden magic, many abilities come with costs or complications that characters might want to hide.

#### What does your character's magic cost them that others can't easily see?

*Physical toll, emotional burden, shortened lifespan, moral compromise?*

[Your answer here]

#### Why do they hide this cost?

*Shame, protection of others, fear of being seen as weak, fear of being stopped?*

[Your answer here]

#### What would the love interest do if they discovered the hidden cost?

*Would they try to stop your character, share the burden, or respect the choice?*

[Your answer here]

## Oaths, Debts & Binding Agreements

Many fantasy worlds include magic that holds people to their word. Bargains, oaths, contracts — these create obligations that can trap characters in impossible situations.

#### What promises in your world are magically enforced?

*What happens when they're broken?*

[Your answer here]

#### Is your character bound by any magical oath or agreement?

*What are the terms, and who holds the other end?*

[Your answer here]

#### Does this binding create an obstacle to the romance?

*Something they've promised that conflicts with what they want?*

[Your answer here]

#### Could a magical bargain be used *for* the romance?

*A binding that protects, legitimizes, or forces proximity? What would the terms be, and who would propose it?*

[Your answer here]

#### What's the most dangerous promise your character could make? What would push them to make it?

*Love makes people offer things they shouldn't. What would your protagonist risk for the one they love?*

[Your answer here]

## Opposition & Incompatibility

Sometimes the magic itself creates conflict — abilities that clash, cancel each other out, or pose genuine danger when brought together.

#### Do your characters' magical abilities conflict?

*What happens when they're used in close proximity — cancellation, amplification, volatility, pain?*

[Your answer here]

#### Is this opposition a permanent state or something that can be overcome?

*What would it take — practice, trust, or sacrifice?*

[Your answer here]

#### How does magical incompatibility mirror or contrast with their personal dynamic?

*Are they opposites in temperament too, or is the magical conflict at odds with their emotional compatibility?*

[Your answer here]

#### If their magic is dangerous to combine, what circumstances might force them to try anyway?

*What would be worth the risk?*

[Your answer here]

## Power Imbalance

Romantic fantasy often pairs characters with vastly different levels of power. The key is making sure the "weaker" character isn't actually powerless.

**How to write it:** Show the imbalance through interaction dynamics. Who waits for whom? Who has to ask permission? Whose comfort is automatically prioritized? The powerful character might not even notice these patterns — that obliviousness is itself revealing. The less powerful character navigates constantly: choosing battles, knowing when to push back and when silence is safer. Write moments where power becomes visible to both of them: the casual display of strength that's meant to impress but actually intimidates, the moment the powerful one realizes how much they could hurt without trying. True romantic tension comes when the powerful character deliberately gives up power — asks instead of commands, waits instead of takes, makes themselves vulnerable despite having every advantage. When the "weaker" character chooses to trust despite knowing what could be done to them, that's intimacy that power imbalance makes possible.

#### Is there a significant power gap between your characters?

*Who holds more magical, political, or physical power?*

[Your answer here]

#### What does the more powerful character have that the other wants or needs?

*What could they give — or withhold?*

[Your answer here]

#### Now flip it: what does the "weaker" character have that the powerful one lacks?

*Knowledge, skills, connections, immunity, moral clarity, the ability to say no?*

[Your answer here]

#### How does the power balance shift throughout your story?

*What moments give the less powerful character the upper hand?*

[Your answer here]

#### What would an outsider see when watching their dynamic?

*Would they be concerned? Are they right to be?*

[Your answer here]

## Magic Used Against Will

The darkest magical conflicts involve power used without consent — abilities that can compel, manipulate, or control.

#### Can your character's magic be used against their will?

*By whom and under what circumstances?*

[Your answer here]

#### Can your character's magic affect others without their consent?

*What are the ethical lines they've drawn — and have they ever crossed them?*

[Your answer here]

#### What magical violation exists in your world that your characters fear most?

*From others, or from themselves?*

[Your answer here]

#### If one character used magic on the other in a morally gray moment — for protection, for information, in desperation — could the relationship survive it?

*What would repair require?*

[Your answer here]

## The World at War: Magic as Structural Pressure

So far, we've focused on how magic creates conflict between your characters — their powers, their secrets, their imbalances. But magic also shapes the larger world your characters live in, and that world exerts its own pressure on their relationship.

Wars fought over magical resources. Political systems built on magical hierarchy. Environmental damage from centuries of spellwork. These aren't personal conflicts, but they create the conditions your characters must navigate — and often force impossible choices between love and duty, safety and conscience, each other and everyone else.

### Magical Resources and Scarcity

If magic requires resources — rare materials, specific locations, limited energy — then someone controls those resources. And someone else wants them.

#### Does magic in your world require resources that can be controlled, hoarded, or fought over?

*Rare plants, minerals, or creatures. Ley lines or places of power. Magical artifacts. Blood or life force. Access to training, texts, or teachers.*

[Your answer here]

#### Who controls magical resources in your world? Who's excluded from access?

*Consider how your protagonist and love interest relate to those in power and those denied power.*

[Your answer here]

#### Are there active conflicts — wars, trade disputes, political maneuvering — over magical resources?

*How do these affect ordinary people?*

[Your answer here]

#### How might resource scarcity or control put pressure on your leads' relationship?

*They're on opposite sides. One controls something the other needs. Their relationship threatens power structures. Staying together requires inaccessible resources.*

[Your answer here]

### Magical Damage and Corruption

Power often leaves marks on the world. Battlefields that won't heal. Corrupted lands. Magical pollution that poisons slowly. The consequences of past magic can shape the present.

#### Has magic damaged your world?

*Are there places, creatures, or people marked by magical catastrophe?*

[Your answer here]

#### Is magical corruption spreading, stable, or being healed?

*What would it take to fix the damage — and what would that cost?*

[Your answer here]

#### Do your characters live with the consequences of magical damage?

*How does it affect their daily lives, communities, futures?*

[Your answer here]

#### Could magical corruption threaten your characters directly?

*Their home, their people, their health, their powers?*

[Your answer here]

### Magical Arms Races

When magic can be weaponized, powers compete to develop stronger magic, better countermeasures, more devastating applications. Your characters may live in a world shaped by this escalation.

#### Is there military or political competition to develop magical power in your world?

*Nations racing to train war-mages. Factions seeking ancient weapons. Attempts to breed more powerful magic users. Magical espionage.*

[Your answer here]

#### What's the most dangerous magical weapon or capability in your world?

*Who has it, and who wants it?*

[Your answer here]

#### Are your characters caught up in this competition?

*As weapons, as soldiers, as prizes, as targets?*

[Your answer here]

#### How might magical militarization put pressure on the relationship?

*They're seen as assets rather than people. Their abilities make them valuable to factions. Love creates vulnerability enemies can exploit. Duties put them on opposite sides.*

[Your answer here]

### Regulation, Control, and Resistance

Governments and institutions don't ignore power. Magic that exists will be regulated, taxed, exploited, or suppressed — and where there's control, there's resistance.

#### How does authority in your world attempt to control magic?

*Registration of magic users. Licensing and restriction. Conscription of powerful mages. Suppression of "dangerous" types. State monopoly on training. Taxation of magical goods.*

[Your answer here]

#### Who benefits from magical regulation? Who suffers under it?

*Where do your leads fall in this divide, and how does that shape their worldview and choices?*

[Your answer here]

#### Is there resistance to magical control?

*Underground magic users, rebel factions, hidden communities, black markets?*

[Your answer here]

#### Where do your characters stand in relation to magical authority?

*Do they enforce it, suffer under it, resist it, exploit it, try to reform it?*

| Character | Position on Magical Authority |
| --- | --- |
| Protagonist (example) | Secretly practices forbidden shadow magic; must hide abilities from the Mage Registry or face execution |
| Protagonist |  |
| Love Interest |  |

#### How might their positions regarding magical authority create tension between them — or force them into alliance?

*Opposing loyalties can become the foundation for enemies-to-lovers or the wedge that keeps them apart.*

[Your answer here]

### History Repeating

The magical conflicts of the past shape the world your characters inherit. Old wars, ancient wrongs, and long-standing power structures don't disappear — they echo.

#### What major magical conflict shaped your world's recent history?

*A war, a catastrophe, a revolution, a conquest?*

[Your answer here]

#### How does that conflict still affect the present?

*What resentments, imbalances, or unfinished business remain?*

[Your answer here]

#### Do your characters come from different sides of this historical divide?

*Inherited enmity creates powerful tension when attraction crosses lines generations have drawn.*

[Your answer here]

#### What would it take to truly resolve the old conflict?

*Is that resolution possible within your story, or is it the wound your world carries?*

[Your answer here]

### The Bigger Pressure

Zoom out for a moment. Think about how the world's magical conflicts — not just your characters' personal magical issues — create pressure on the romance.

#### What external magical conflict puts the most pressure on your leads' relationship?

*The world's problems should intrude on personal happiness, forcing impossible choices.*

[Your answer here]

#### At some point, will your characters have to choose between each other and the larger conflict?

*What does that choice look like?*

[Your answer here]

#### If they ignore the world's problems to be together, what happens?

*Can they live with the consequences?*

[Your answer here]

#### If they sacrifice their relationship to address the world's problems, what happens?

*Would either of them actually make that choice?*

[Your answer here]

> ### Final Thought: Magic Should Complicate, Not Just Enable
>
> The best romantic fantasy uses magic as both solution and problem. Your magic system should create as many obstacles as it removes. Every ability comes with a cost, a limitation, a social consequence, or a danger.
>
> Ask yourself: What problems does magic create for my characters that they couldn't have without it? The answer to that question is where your most interesting conflict lives.
>
> Magic that only helps is boring. Magic that helps and hurts, that grants power and demands sacrifice, that connects and divides — that's the magic that makes romantasy work.

## Section 13: The Pressure Cooker — Forced Proximity by Design

You've already built geography that isolates (Section 1) and institutions that bind (Section 14). This section is about *using* those elements to create sustained proximity — settings that function as pressure systems, compressing your characters together until avoiding each other becomes impossible.

The "only one bed" trope works because it removes the option of avoidance. In romantasy, you can scale this principle up to entire settings — academies where students share dorms, ships where passengers can't escape each other, journeys through dangerous terrain where separation means death.

> ### Pressure Cooker Settings Do Three Crucial Things
>
> 1. **Remove the option to leave** — Characters are trapped together by geography, obligation, or danger
> 2. **Force constant interaction** — Privacy is limited; they see each other daily (or constantly)
> 3. **Accelerate intimacy** — Compressed proximity speeds up relationship development that might take months in normal circumstances

This section helps you design how your setting functions as a pressure system — not just where your characters are trapped, but *how* that entrapment forces them to confront their feelings, conflicts, and attraction.

## In This Section

### Core Concepts

- [The Core Principle: Why They Can't Leave](#s13-core-principle)
- [Physical Pressure vs. Emotional Pressure](#s13-physical-emotional)
- [Your Pressure Cooker Setting](#s13-setting)

### People & Dynamics

- [Other People in the Pressure Cooker](#s13-other-people)
- [Forced Interaction Points](#s13-forced-interaction)
- [Routines & Rhythms](#s13-routines)

### Tension & Change

- [Relief & Breathing Room](#s13-relief)
- [Escalating the Pressure](#s13-escalating)
- [How Confinement Changes Them](#s13-confinement-changes)

### Design & Synthesis

- [Scaling Proximity](#s13-scaling)
- [Privacy Within Proximity](#s13-privacy)
- [The Diagnostic Question](#s13-diagnostic)
- [Integration Check](#s13-integration)
- [Quick Reference](#s13-quick-ref)

### The Core Principle: Why They Can't Leave

Before anything else, answer this: **What prevents your characters from simply avoiding each other?**

The strongest pressure cookers have multiple layers of constraint:

#### Physical constraints

*Geography, architecture, locked doors*

[Your answer here]

#### Obligation

*Must complete a task, fulfill a contract, serve a sentence*

[Your answer here]

#### Danger

*Can't survive alone, enemies surround them, wilderness is lethal*

[Your answer here]

#### Social/political requirements

*Must maintain appearances, fulfill duties*

[Your answer here]

#### Economic necessity

*Job requires it, only shelter available, debt binding them*

[Your answer here]

#### Magical binding

*Curse, bond, spell requires proximity*

[Your answer here]

#### How long are they trapped together?

*Days, weeks, months? The duration shapes whether intimacy builds slowly or ignites under pressure.*

[Your answer here]

#### Can they physically separate within the confined space?

*Can they retreat to separate rooms, or are they truly stuck in close quarters?*

[Your answer here]

#### What happens if they try to leave or separate?

*Death? Failure? Social ruin? Magical backlash? Be specific about consequences.*

[Your answer here]

### Physical Pressure vs. Emotional Pressure

Physical constraints are obvious — walls, geography, locks. But emotional stakes can make leaving feel impossible even when it's technically possible.

#### Beyond physical constraints, what emotional stakes keep them there?

*Would leaving mean abandoning someone who needs them? Admitting defeat? Breaking a promise? Losing their only chance at something they need?*

[Your answer here]

#### Could either character technically leave but chooses to stay?

*If yes — why do they stay? What would leaving cost them emotionally?*

[Your answer here]

#### What would leaving say about them — to themselves and each other?

*Would it mean they're a coward? That they don't care? That they've given up?*

[Your answer here]

#### Is there a moment when one considers leaving but doesn't?

*What stops them — the physical constraints, or something deeper?*

[Your answer here]

### Your Pressure Cooker Setting

You've likely already identified your setting in Section 1 (Geography) or Section 14 (Institutions). Now define how it functions as a pressure system.

#### What is your primary pressure cooker setting?

*Reference: isolated locations from Section 1, institutional settings from Section 14*

[Your answer here]

#### Map the constraints:

| Constraint Type | Specific Details |
| --- | --- |
| Time pressure (example) | Must complete the bonding ritual before the spring equinox or lose claim to the throne; only 6 weeks remain |
| External threat (example) | Enemy army three months away; alliance marriage to the rival kingdom's prince is the only way to secure reinforcements |
| Physical (size, layout, barriers) |  |
| Temporal (how long they're stuck) |  |
| Survival (needs that must be met) |  |
| Social (who's watching, what's expected) |  |
| Escape (what happens if they try to leave) |  |
|  |  |
|  |  |

#### What's the minimum physical distance they can maintain?

*Can they stay in separate buildings? Separate rooms? Or are they sharing space constantly?*

[Your answer here]

### Other People in the Pressure Cooker

Forced proximity rarely means just the two of them. Others in the space change everything — creating audience, competition, threat, or alliance.

#### Who else is present in the confined setting?

*Allies, rivals, authority figures, servants? Others shape what your leads can say and do around each other.*

[Your answer here]

#### How do others affect how the protagonists can interact?

*Must they hide their feelings? Maintain appearances? Compete for attention? Perform a relationship that isn't real (yet)?*

[Your answer here]

#### Is there a rival for either character's attention?

*Someone else interested in one of them? A former lover present? Someone they're "supposed" to be with?*

[Your answer here]

#### Is there an ally who helps them find private moments?

*Someone who covers for them, creates distractions, keeps secrets?*

[Your answer here]

#### Is there a threat — someone who would expose or harm them?

*Someone watching, someone who would report them, someone dangerous?*

[Your answer here]

#### What can't they say or do because others are present?

*The words they swallow and the touches they deny create tension that demands eventual release.*

[Your answer here]

#### What happens when they're finally alone — truly alone — for the first time?

*After constant company, the first real privacy:*

[Your answer here]

### Relief & Breathing Room

Constant pressure isn't sustainable — for characters or readers. Moments of relief make the pressure meaningful by contrast.

### Escalating the Pressure

Pressure should increase over time, not remain static. The container should tighten.

#### Initial proximity level:

*How close are they forced to be at the start?*

#### What increases the pressure over time?

*Consider: Space gets smaller, time gets shorter, stakes get higher, others leave so they're more alone, danger increases, walls between them (literal or figurative) come down.*

[Your answer here]

### How Confinement Changes Them

Proximity reveals things distance hides. Stress brings out truth. By the end of confinement, they should know each other differently than they did at the start.

#### What does proximity reveal about each character that distance would have hidden?

**About the protagonist** (habits, fears, kindness, flaws, vulnerabilities):

[Your answer here]

**About the love interest:**
